< text>
I've been coming here since I was a little kid, pretty much all my life, many many years. I used to get my haircut by Mario before he retired. The haircuts have always been great! I can't find anywhere else that gives them better, especially by Eddie, the man at the back of the shop. Been coming to him for years now. But in the past 2 years, the experience there has REALLY declined. Despite the "NO FOUL LANGUAGE" signs, it doesn't stop the employees from using foul language. Many times, loud verbal fights break out among the employees (who are mostly family), which makes it very awkward and uncomfortable for all the customers silently watching on. And professionalism has become an issue: employees not showing up on time, not being there, old buddies coming in just to hang out and drink beer, etc. And one more thing.. I know they have kids and have to take care of them, I get it, and I don't expect them to drop their kids because of their jobs. But there ARE solutions to this. The kids have become a huge distraction for the employees, not enabling them to work properly, and from time to time, even having to discipline them in front of everyone.
So, I write this, not because I'm spiteful or mad (I love the people who work there and have known them for many years), but because I want them to know what their business looks like through the eyes of a customer, so they can find solutions to these issues, and become even better than they are.
I say try them out at least once. Their hair cutting skills are the best. But the atmosphere is not one I want to be around. As for me, I think I'll find somewhere else to go from now on.< /text>

<Rating>1<//Rating>< text>
Parking $20, cash only. Not well organized. The bathrooms are horrendous. I was less worried about COVID and more worried about sepsis. $25 per person for entry for the day. You get a colored wristband. Sledding slopes are fun, there are 4 in all. We were later told that they were going to do a "COVID count", meaning that if they had admitted too many people, those with a specific color of wristband would be asked to leave. So basically, you could travel there, pay for parking, pay for entry, go sledding for an hour and then be asked to leave because they let in too many people. Their policy, apparently, is to collect as many daily entrance fees as possible without regard to the fact that people paid for admittance for the whole day.  Did I mention the bathrooms?</text>

<date>1543708530141<//date>< text>
Went with family after a fresh powder. Kids wanted to snow sled, this place charges $10 to park your car and then another $10 per person to use the slopes, there was lots of fresh snow and place looked very spacious with medium elevation that kids can easily handle.

However there is no easy pathway to trek high up for the sled to have enough downgrade push to slide. Kids trekked halfway up in waist deep snow to no avail. There was a side pathway that seemed heated or framed and seemed sturdy enough to trek up higher , we trekked towards it and tried to use it to go further up,  but the attendants started yelling from down below to not use that. Apparently that is only or employees.

So then how are people able to go high enough to able to use sled or tubes. Walked back down to ticket counter after 10 - 15 minutes of struggling in snow and talked to the ticket counter lady on why can't we be allowed to use the sturdy path to go up higher ,and the answer was sorry we can't. When I asked her on how do she suggest that we go up high enough to sled, she mentioned sorry its fresh snow and its not ideal condition for sledding or tubing. When i asked that why we weren't told prior to paying that sledding or tubing may not be feasible that day due to fresh powder, there was no answer but sorry. No refund.

Be aware and make sure that you check conditions are ideal before you pay to use the slopes. I did the mistake of not realizing that and assuming that they would have a way for their patrons to get higher enough on the slopes and enjoy the place, but i was sorely mistaken.</text>

<gmapID>0x80ecf10227ec71ab:0x55baa6ecd7755a7c< /gmapID><resp>None</resp>< Rate>
2<//Rate>
<text>Something has gone horribly wrong. The place is located in a historic Chinatown district, and they've been open since the 1800s apparently. I suspect that it's only still around due to tradition. All the employees seem to be Caucasian.

I ordered the noodle soup and it tasted exactly like the fake Asian soup I try to make. Way too much cilantro. Way too much white pepper.  The soup stock tasted ultra-processed. And most of all, the noodles tasted like regular pasta.  I just found it really amusing and disappointing that the soup tasted exactly like the kind I make as a regular guy who knows nothing about Asian cooking trying to emulate it.  It tasted okay at least.

The lo mein, though. I got the chili peanut sauce, and something just tasted horrible at the very beginning. Almost toxic. I couldn't finish it. My dad said it tasted like it was from a can. But it was really offensive to me. I feel like I wasted $28. I don't think it deserves to be considered an Asian restaurant anymore. I really wish I could get my money back.

The second star is for the almond cookies. They were really good.  They were more like ginger cookies though with a lot of baking soda.  One guy told us they were $0.75. All of the storage facilities closer to our house were not climate controlled, cost more & usually drive-up type.  (We had a drive up storage in Spokane & although it can be easier, it was humid & musky even though it was a brand new facility. Plus we had so many bugs at that one!) < Text>
I am very disappointed in my experience here. When I got my storage, I was not told that in 6 months, the price would increase 20%, which is almost a $60 increase for my storage unit. I've rented many storages in the past, including a different Public Storage, and I've never experienced this. Some storages such as U-Haul actually decreased the rate after a certain period as an incentive to keep customers who pay on time. When I called the corporate office to express my concerns, the representative told me that the contract I signed says, "subject to change" and therefore they are able to make an "executive decision" to raise rates 20%. This forces many customers to downsize (where the price will again increase in 6 months) or pay the higher rate, as it is a huge hassle to rent a truck and movers to move to a new storage. I feel that this practice is very unethical. I would not recommend this storage - there are many nice storages in the Gardena/ Redondo Beach area without this policy. It may also be helpful to look at the reviews of this storage on Yelp.< /Text>

Andrea and Mike were the example of quality customer service. Thank you for exemplifying the Twelve Best Practices of Customer Service.

"The twelve best practices are found in companies that exemplify excellent customer service. These practices are not just something the company does, the practices are the company. Every employee in the company must understand and carry out these practices on a daily basis. Hiring people with the right attitudes and keeping them constantly trained, rewarded and recognized for demonstrating the best of these twelve practices is the way that companies achieve success. It is essential that the top person in the organization, CEO or owner also demonstrate these practices; not just among external customers, but among those internal customers, especially employees. Remembering that happy employees make happy customers is a critical bit of advice for every chief executive."

Richard C. Whiteley, The Forum Corporation, 1991< /Review>
